Accretion early in the history of Mars is plausible, but would not account for a composition resembling asteroids rather than Mars itself, if that is confirmed.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-208) Mars may have yet-undiscovered moons, smaller than 50 to 100 metres (160 to 330 ft) in diameter, and a dust ring is predicted to exist between Phobos and Deimos.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-adler-209)

A third possibility for their origin as satellites of Mars is the involvement of a third body or a type of impact disruption. More-recent lines of evidence for Phobos having a highly porous interior,[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Andert-210) and suggesting a composition containing mainly [phyllosilicates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phyllosilicates "Phyllosilicates") and other minerals known from Mars,[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Giuranna-211) point toward an origin of Phobos from material ejected by an impact on Mars that reaccreted in Martian orbit, similar to the [prevailing theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giant_impact_hypothesis "Giant impact hypothesis") for the origin of Earth's satellite. Although the [visible and near-infrared](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visible_and_near-infrared "Visible and near-infrared") (VNIR) spectra of the moons of Mars resemble those of outer-belt asteroids, the [thermal infrared](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_infrared "Thermal infrared") spectra of Phobos are reported to be inconsistent with [chondrites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chondrite "Chondrite") of any class.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Giuranna-211) It is also possible that Phobos and Deimos were fragments of an older moon, formed by debris from a large impact on Mars, and then destroyed by a more recent impact upon the satellite.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-212)

Human observations and exploration
----------------------------------

The history of observations of Mars is marked by oppositions of Mars when the planet is closest to Earth and hence is most easily visible, which occur every couple of years. Even more notable are the [perihelic oppositions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perihelic_opposition "Perihelic opposition") of Mars, which are distinguished because Mars is close to perihelion, making it even closer to Earth.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-:1-198)

### Ancient observations

The ancient [Sumerians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumer "Sumer") named Mars [Nergal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nergal "Nergal"), the god of war and plague. During Sumerian times, Nergal was a minor deity of little significance, but, during later times, his main cult center was the city of [Nineveh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nineveh "Nineveh").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Rabkin2005-213) In Mesopotamian texts, Mars is referred to as the "star of judgement of the fate of the dead".[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-214) The existence of Mars as a wandering object in the night sky was also recorded by the ancient [Egyptian astronomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_astronomy "Egyptian astronomy") and, by 1534 BCE, they were familiar with the [retrograde motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_retrograde_motion "Apparent retrograde motion") of the planet.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-paob85-215) By the period of the [Neo-Babylonian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Babylonian_Empire "Neo-Babylonian Empire"), the [Babylonian astronomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_astronomy "Babylonian astronomy") were making regular records of the positions of the planets and systematic observations of their behavior. For Mars, they knew that the planet made 37 [synodic periods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_period "Orbital period"), or 42 circuits of the zodiac, every 79 years. They invented arithmetic methods for making minor corrections to the predicted positions of the planets.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-north08-216)[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-swerdlow98-217) In [Ancient Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece"), the planet was known as [Πυρόεις](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyroeis "Pyroeis").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-218) Commonly, the Greek name for the planet now referred to as Mars, was Ares. It was the Romans who named the planet Mars, for their god of war, often represented by the sword and shield of the planet's namesake.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-219)

In the fourth century BCE, [Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") noted that Mars disappeared behind the Moon during an [occultation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occultation "Occultation"), indicating that the planet was farther away.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-220)[Ptolemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ptolemy "Ptolemy"), a Greek living in [Alexandria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexandria "Alexandria"),[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-harland-221) attempted to address the problem of the orbital motion of Mars. Ptolemy's model and his collective work on astronomy was presented in the multi-volume collection later called the _[Almagest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almagest "Almagest")_ (from the Arabic for "greatest"), which became the authoritative treatise on [Western astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_astronomy "Medieval astronomy") for the next fourteen centuries.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-222) Literature from ancient China confirms that Mars was known by [Chinese astronomers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_astronomy "Chinese astronomy") by no later than the fourth century BCE.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-needham_ronan85-223) In the [East Asian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asian "East Asian") cultures, Mars is traditionally referred to as the "fire star" based on the [_Wuxing_ system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wuxing_(Chinese_philosophy) "Wuxing (Chinese philosophy)").[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-224)[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-225)[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-226)

### Early modern observations

[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Kepler_Mars_retrograde.jpg/250px-Kepler_Mars_retrograde.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kepler_Mars_retrograde.jpg)

Diagram of the [geocentric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocentric "Geocentric") trajectory of Mars through several periods of [apparent retrograde motion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_retrograde_motion "Apparent retrograde motion") in [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler")'s _Astronomia Nova_ (1609)

In 1609 [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler") published a 10 year study of Martian orbit,[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-v529-227) using the [diurnal parallax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diurnal_parallax "Diurnal parallax") of Mars, measured by [Tycho Brahe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tycho_Brahe "Tycho Brahe"), to make a preliminary calculation of the relative distance to the planet.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-taton03-228) From Brahe's observations of Mars, Kepler deduced that the planet orbited the Sun not in a circle, but in an [ellipse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellipse "Ellipse"). Moreover, Kepler showed that Mars sped up as it approached the Sun and slowed down as it moved farther away, in a manner that later physicists would explain as a consequence of the [conservation of angular momentum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_of_angular_momentum "Conservation of angular momentum").[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-TMU-229): 433–437

[![Image 20](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Lowell_-_Mars_%281894%29_-_Huyghens%27_drawing_of_the_Syrtis_Major%2C_Nov._28%2C_1659.jpg/250px-Lowell_-_Mars_%281894%29_-_Huyghens%27_drawing_of_the_Syrtis_Major%2C_Nov._28%2C_1659.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lowell_-_Mars_(1894)_-_Huyghens%27_drawing_of_the_Syrtis_Major,_Nov._28,_1659.jpg)

First drawn record of Martian features (Manuscript K), by [Christiaan Huygens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens "Christiaan Huygens"), observed on the 28th of November 1659.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-v462-230) The feature is probably [Syrtis Major Planum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrtis_Major_Planum "Syrtis Major Planum"). Huygens calculated from the moving of the features the rotation of Mars.

In 1610 the first use of a telescope for astronomical observation, including Mars, was performed by Italian astronomer [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei").[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-jha15-231) With the telescope the diurnal parallax of Mars was again measured in an effort to determine the Sun-Earth distance. This was first performed by [Giovanni Domenico Cassini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Domenico_Cassini "Giovanni Domenico Cassini") in 1672. The early parallax measurements were hampered by the quality of the instruments.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-hirschfeld01-232) The only [occultation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occultation "Occultation") of Mars by Venus observed was that of 13 October 1590, seen by [Michael Maestlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Maestlin "Michael Maestlin") at [Heidelberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heidelberg "Heidelberg").[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-sat57-233)

### Martian "canals"

[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mars_-_MEC-1_Prototype._LOC_2013593160.jpg/500px-Mars_-_MEC-1_Prototype._LOC_2013593160.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mars_-_MEC-1_Prototype._LOC_2013593160.jpg)

A 1962 map of Mars published by the U.S. [Aeronautical Chart and Information Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeronautical_Chart_and_Information_Center "Aeronautical Chart and Information Center"), showing canals snaking through the Martian landscape. At the time, the existence of canals was still highly controversial as no close-up pictures of Mars had been taken (until [Mariner 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_4 "Mariner 4")'s flyby in 1965).

By the 19th century, the resolution of telescopes reached a level sufficient for surface features to be identified. On 5 September 1877, a perihelic opposition to Mars occurred. The Italian astronomer [Giovanni Schiaparelli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Schiaparelli "Giovanni Schiaparelli") used a 22-centimetre (8.7 in) telescope in [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan "Milan") to help produce the first detailed map of Mars. These maps notably contained features he called _canali_, which, with the possible exception of the natural canyon [Valles Marineris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valles_Marineris "Valles Marineris"), were later shown to be an [optical illusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_illusion "Optical illusion"). These _canali_ were supposedly long, straight lines on the surface of Mars, to which he gave names of famous rivers on Earth. His term, which means "channels" or "grooves", was popularly mistranslated in English as "canals".[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-234)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-sagan80-235)

Influenced by the observations, the orientalist [Percival Lowell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Percival_Lowell "Percival Lowell") founded [an observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lowell_Observatory "Lowell Observatory") which had 30- and 45-centimetre (12- and 18-in) telescopes. The observatory was used for the exploration of Mars during the last good opportunity in 1894, and the following less favorable oppositions. He published several books on Mars and life on the planet, which had a great influence on the public.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-basalla06-236)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-NYT-20151001-237) The _canali_ were independently observed by other astronomers, like [Henri Joseph Perrotin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_Joseph_Perrotin "Henri Joseph Perrotin") and [Louis Thollon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Thollon "Louis Thollon") in Nice, using one of the largest telescopes of that time.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-maria_lane05-238)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-ba3-239)

The seasonal changes (consisting of the diminishing of the polar caps and the dark areas formed during Martian summers) in combination with the canals led to speculation about life on Mars, and it was a long-held belief that Mars contained vast seas and vegetation. As bigger telescopes were used, fewer long, straight _canali_ were observed. During observations in 1909 by [Antoniadi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoniadi "Antoniadi") with an 84-centimetre (33 in) telescope, irregular patterns were observed, but no _canali_ were seen.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-zahnle01-240)

### Robotic exploration

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/M04_12.jpg/250px-M04_12.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:M04_12.jpg)

The very first two images from, and of, another planet (Mars), by [Mariner 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_4 "Mariner 4"),[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-u445-241) the second spacecraft to reach Mars and the first to transmit data (15 July 1965). The data disproved Mars being hospitable and having canals.

Dozens of crewless [spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft"), including [orbiters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbiter "Orbiter"), [landers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_lander "Mars lander"), and [rovers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_rover "Mars rover"), have been sent to Mars by the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_space_program "Soviet space program"), the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA"), [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESA "ESA"), [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISRO "ISRO"), the [United Arab Emirates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Rashid_Space_Centre "Mohammed bin Rashid Space Centre"), and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNSA "CNSA") to study the planet's surface, climate, and geology.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-242) NASA's _Mariner 4_ was the first spacecraft to visit Mars; launched on 28 November 1964, it made its closest approach to the planet on 15 July 1965. _Mariner 4_ detected the weak Martian radiation belt, measured at about 0.1% that of Earth, and captured the first images of another planet from deep space.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-243)

Once [spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft") visited the planet during NASA's [Mariner missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_program "Mariner program") in the 1960s and 1970s, many previous concepts of Mars were radically broken. After the results of the _Viking_ life-detection experiments, the hypothesis of a dead planet was generally accepted.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-ward_brownlee00-244) The data from _Mariner 9_ and _Viking_ allowed better maps of Mars to be made, and the _[Mars Global Surveyor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Global\_Surveyor "Mars Global Surveyor")_ mission, which launched in 1996 and operated until late 2006, produced complete, extremely detailed maps of the Martian topography, magnetic field and surface minerals.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Distant_worlds:_milestones_in_planetary_exploration-245) These maps are available online at websites including [Google Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Mars "Google Mars"). Both the _[Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Reconnaissance\_Orbiter "Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter")_ and _[Mars Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Express "Mars Express")_ continued exploring with new instruments and supporting lander missions. NASA provides two online tools: Mars Trek, which provides visualizations of the planet using data from 50 years of exploration, and [Experience Curiosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Experience_Curiosity "Experience Curiosity"), which simulates traveling on Mars in 3-D with _Curiosity_.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-246)[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-247)

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Mars_2020_selfie_containing_both_perseverance_rover_and_ingenuity.gif/500px-Mars_2020_selfie_containing_both_perseverance_rover_and_ingenuity.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mars_2020_selfie_containing_both_perseverance_rover_and_ingenuity.gif)

[Self-portrait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-portrait "Self-portrait") of _[Perseverance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perseverance\_(rover) "Perseverance (rover)")_ rover and _[Ingenuity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ingenuity\_(helicopter) "Ingenuity (helicopter)")_ helicopter (left) at [Wright Brothers Field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wright_Brothers_Field "Wright Brothers Field"), 2021

As of 2023, Mars is host to ten functioning [spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft"). Eight are in orbit _: [2001 Mars Odyssey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001\_Mars\_Odyssey "2001 Mars Odyssey")_, _[Mars Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Express "Mars Express")_, _[Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars\_Reconnaissance\_Orbiter "Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter")_, _[MAVEN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MAVEN "MAVEN")_, _[ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ExoMars\_Trace\_Gas\_Orbiter "ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter")_, the _[Hope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirates\_Mars\_Mission "Emirates Mars Mission")_ orbiter, and the _[Tianwen-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tianwen-1 "Tianwen-1")_ orbiter.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-248)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-249) Another two are on the surface: the [Mars Science Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory "Mars Science Laboratory")_[Curiosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curiosity\_(rover) "Curiosity (rover)")_ rover and the _[Perseverance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perseverance\_(rover) "Perseverance (rover)")_ rover.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-nyt-china-2021-250)

Planned missions to Mars include:

*   NASA's [EscaPADE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EscaPADE "EscaPADE") spacecraft, planned to launch in 2025.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-nasa2024062024-251)
*   The [_Rosalind Franklin_ rover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rosalind_Franklin_(rover) "Rosalind Franklin (rover)") mission, designed to search for evidence of past life, which was intended to be launched in 2018 but has been repeatedly delayed, with a launch date pushed to 2028 at the earliest.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-252)[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-253)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-254) The project was restarted in 2024 with additional funding.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-255)
*   A current concept for a joint [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA")-[ESA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Space_Agency "European Space Agency") mission to [return samples from Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA-ESA_Mars_Sample_Return "NASA-ESA Mars Sample Return") would launch in 2026.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-256)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-257)
*   China's [Tianwen-3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tianwen-3 "Tianwen-3"), a sample return mission, scheduled to launch in 2030.

As of February 2024, debris from these types of missions has reached over seven tons. Most of it consists of crashed and inactive spacecraft as well as discarded components.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-258)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-259)

In April 2024, NASA selected several companies to begin studies on providing commercial services to further enable robotic science on Mars. Key areas include establishing telecommunications, payload delivery and surface imaging.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-260)

### Habitability and the search for life

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-Sol170%2B%2B-2.jpg/330px-MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-Sol170%2B%2B-2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:MarsCuriosityRover-Drilling-Sol170%2B%2B-2.jpg)

_[Curiosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curiosity\_(rover) "Curiosity (rover)")_ rover's robotic arm showing drill in place, February 2013

During the late 19th century, it was widely accepted in the astronomical community that Mars had life-supporting qualities, including the presence of oxygen and water.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-CampbellWW-261) However, in 1894 [W. W. Campbell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Wallace_Campbell "William Wallace Campbell") at [Lick Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lick_Observatory "Lick Observatory") observed the planet and found that "if water vapor or oxygen occur in the atmosphere of Mars it is in quantities too small to be detected by spectroscopes then available".[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-CampbellWW-261) That observation contradicted many of the measurements of the time and was not widely accepted.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-CampbellWW-261) Campbell and [V. M. Slipher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vesto_Slipher "Vesto Slipher") repeated the study in 1909 using better instruments, but with the same results. It was not until the findings were confirmed by [W. S. Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Sydney_Adams "Walter Sydney Adams") in 1925 that the myth of the Earth-like habitability of Mars was finally broken.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-CampbellWW-261) However, even in the 1960s, articles were published on Martian biology, putting aside explanations other than life for the seasonal changes on Mars.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-science136_3510-262)

The current understanding of [planetary habitability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability")– the ability of a world to develop environmental conditions favorable to the emergence of life– favors planets that have liquid water on their surface. Most often this requires the orbit of a planet to lie within the [habitable zone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumstellar_habitable_zone "Circumstellar habitable zone"), which for the Sun is estimated to extend from within the orbit of Earth to about that of Mars.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Kopparapu2013b-263) During perihelion, Mars dips inside this region, but Mars's thin (low-pressure) atmosphere prevents liquid water from existing over large regions for extended periods. The past flow of liquid water demonstrates the planet's potential for habitability. Recent evidence has suggested that any water on the Martian surface may have been too salty and acidic to support regular terrestrial life.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-saltlife-264)

The environmental conditions on Mars are a challenge to sustaining organic life: the planet has little [heat transfer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_transfer "Heat transfer") across its surface, it has poor insulation against [bombardment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind#Atmospheres "Solar wind") by the [solar wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind") due to the absence of a magnetosphere and has insufficient atmospheric pressure to retain water in a liquid form (water instead [sublimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sublimation_(phase_transition) "Sublimation (phase transition)") to a gaseous state). Mars is nearly, or perhaps totally, geologically dead; the end of volcanic activity has apparently stopped the recycling of chemicals and minerals between the surface and interior of the planet.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-hannsson97-265)

Evidence suggests that the planet was once significantly more habitable than it is today, but whether living [organisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organism "Organism") ever existed there remains unknown. The [_Viking_ probes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viking_probes "Viking probes") of the mid-1970s carried experiments designed to detect microorganisms in Martian soil at their respective landing sites and had positive results, including a temporary increase in CO 2 production on exposure to water and nutrients. This sign of life was later disputed by scientists, resulting in a continuing debate, with NASA scientist [Gilbert Levin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilbert_Levin "Gilbert Levin") asserting that _Viking_ may have found life.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-nytobit-266) A 2014 analysis of Martian meteorite EETA79001 found [chlorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorate "Chlorate"), [perchlorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perchlorate "Perchlorate"), and [nitrate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrate "Nitrate") ions in sufficiently high concentrations to suggest that they are widespread on Mars. UV and X-ray radiation would turn chlorate and perchlorate ions into other, highly [reactive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redox "Redox")[oxychlorines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxyanion "Oxyanion"), indicating that any organic molecules would have to be buried under the surface to survive.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-267)

Small quantities of [methane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methane "Methane") and [formaldehyde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formaldehyde "Formaldehyde") detected by Mars orbiters are both claimed to be possible evidence for life, as these [chemical compounds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_compound "Chemical compound") would quickly break down in the Martian atmosphere.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-icarus172-268)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-form-269) Alternatively, these compounds may instead be replenished by volcanic or other geological means, such as [serpentinite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serpentinite "Serpentinite").[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-olivine-129)[Impact glass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impactite "Impactite"), formed by the impact of meteors, which on Earth can preserve signs of life, has also been found on the surface of the impact craters on Mars.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-brown20140418-270)[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-Schultz2014-271) Likewise, the glass in impact craters on Mars could have preserved signs of life, if life existed at the site.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-nasapr20150608-272)[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-brown20150608-273)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-sciam20150612-274)

The [Cheyava Falls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cheyava_Falls "Cheyava Falls") rock discovered on Mars in June 2024 has been designated by NASA as a "potential [biosignature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosignature "Biosignature")" and was core sampled by the [Perseverance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perseverance_(rover) "Perseverance (rover)") rover for possible return to Earth and further examination. Although highly intriguing, no definitive final determination on a biological or abiotic origin of this rock can be made with the data currently available.

### Human mission proposals

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/NextSTEP_mars-soil-excavation.jpg/330px-NextSTEP_mars-soil-excavation.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NextSTEP_mars-soil-excavation.jpg)

A NASA [ISRU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISRU "ISRU") system concept for autonomous robotic excavation and processing of Mars soil to extract water for use in exploration missions.

Several plans for a [human mission to Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars "Human mission to Mars") have been proposed, but none have come to fruition. The NASA Authorization Act of 2017 directed NASA to study the feasibility of a crewed Mars mission in the early 2030s; the resulting report concluded that this would be unfeasible.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-275)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-276) In addition, in 2021, China was planning to send a crewed Mars mission in 2033.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-277)[Privately held companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_spaceflight "Private spaceflight") such as [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX") have also [proposed plans to send humans to Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_Mars_Colonization_Program "SpaceX Mars Colonization Program"), with the eventual goal to [settle on the planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization_of_Mars "Colonization of Mars").[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-278) As of 2024, SpaceX has proceeded with the development of the [Starship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_Starship "SpaceX Starship") launch vehicle with the goal of Mars colonization. In plans shared with the company in April 2024, Elon Musk envisions the beginning of a Mars colony within the next twenty years. This would be enabled by the planned [mass manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_manufacturing "Mass manufacturing") of Starship and initially sustained by resupply from Earth, and [in situ resource utilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_situ_resource_utilization "In situ resource utilization") on Mars, until the Mars colony reaches full self sustainability.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-279) Any future human mission to Mars will likely take place within [the optimal Mars launch window](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars#Launch_windows "Exploration of Mars"), which occurs every 26 months. The moon Phobos has been proposed as an anchor point for a [space elevator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_elevator "Space elevator").[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-280) Besides national space agencies and space companies, groups such as the [Mars Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Society "Mars Society")[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-281) and [The Planetary Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Planetary_Society "The Planetary Society")[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-282) advocate for human missions to Mars.

In culture
----------

[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/War-of-the-worlds-tripod.jpg/250px-War-of-the-worlds-tripod.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:War-of-the-worlds-tripod.jpg)

_[The War of the Worlds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_War\_of\_the\_Worlds "The War of the Worlds")_ by [H. G. Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells"), 1897, depicts an [invasion of Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alien_invasion "Alien invasion") by fictional Martians.

Mars is named after the [Roman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome")[god of war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_(mythology) "Mars (mythology)") ([Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_mythology "Greek mythology")[Ares](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ares "Ares")), but was also associated with the demi-god [Heracles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heracles "Heracles") (Roman [Hercules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hercules "Hercules")) by ancient Greek astronomers, as detailed by [Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle").[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-DRGA_Planetae-283) This association between Mars and war dates back at least to [Babylonian astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonian_astronomy "Babylonian astronomy"), in which the planet was named for the god [Nergal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nergal "Nergal"), deity of war and destruction.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-284)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-285) It persisted into modern times, as exemplified by [Gustav Holst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Holst "Gustav Holst")'s orchestral suite _[The Planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Planets "The Planets")_, whose famous first movement labels Mars "the bringer of war".[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-286)[The planet's symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet_symbols "Planet symbols"), a circle with a spear pointing out to the upper right, is also used as a symbol for the male gender.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-287) The symbol dates from at least the 11th century, though a possible predecessor has been found in the Greek [Oxyrhynchus Papyri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxyrhynchus_Papyri "Oxyrhynchus Papyri").[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-jones-1999-288)

The idea that Mars was populated by intelligent [Martians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martian "Martian") became widespread in the late 19th century. [Schiaparelli's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Schiaparelli "Giovanni Schiaparelli") "canali" observations combined with [Percival Lowell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Percival_Lowell "Percival Lowell")'s books on the subject put forward the standard notion of a planet that was a drying, cooling, dying world with ancient civilizations constructing irrigation works.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-289) Many other observations and proclamations by notable personalities added to what has been termed "Mars Fever".[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-fergus04-290) In the present day, high-resolution mapping of the surface of Mars has revealed no artifacts of habitation, but pseudoscientific speculation about intelligent life on Mars still continues. Reminiscent of the _canali_ observations, these speculations are based on small scale features perceived in the spacecraft images, such as "pyramids" and the "[Face on Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cydonia_(Mars) "Cydonia (Mars)")".[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-291) In his book _[Cosmos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmos\_(Sagan\_book) "Cosmos (Sagan book)")_, planetary astronomer [Carl Sagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Sagan "Carl Sagan") wrote: "Mars has become a kind of mythic arena onto which we have projected our Earthly hopes and fears."[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-sagan80-235)

The depiction of Mars in fiction has been stimulated by its dramatic red color and by nineteenth-century scientific speculations that its surface conditions might support not just life but intelligent life.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-lightman97-292) This gave way to many [science fiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_fiction "Science fiction") stories involving these concepts, such as [H. G. Wells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells")'s _[The War of the Worlds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_War\_of\_the\_Worlds "The War of the Worlds")_, in which Martians seek to escape their dying planet by invading Earth; [Ray Bradbury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Bradbury "Ray Bradbury")'s _[The Martian Chronicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Martian\_Chronicles "The Martian Chronicles")_, in which human explorers accidentally destroy a Martian civilization; as well as [Edgar Rice Burroughs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_Rice_Burroughs "Edgar Rice Burroughs")'s series _[Barsoom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barsoom "Barsoom")_, [C. S. Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C._S._Lewis "C. S. Lewis")'s novel _[Out of the Silent Planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Out\_of\_the\_Silent\_Planet "Out of the Silent Planet")_ (1938),[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-sanford09-293) and a number of [Robert A. Heinlein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_A._Heinlein "Robert A. Heinlein") stories before the mid-sixties.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-buker02-294) Since then, depictions of Martians have also extended to animation. A comic figure of an intelligent Martian, [Marvin the Martian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marvin_the_Martian "Marvin the Martian"), appeared in _[Haredevil Hare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haredevil\_Hare "Haredevil Hare")_ (1948) as a character in the [Looney Tunes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Looney_Tunes "Looney Tunes") animated cartoons of [Warner Brothers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Brothers "Warner Brothers"), and has continued as part of popular culture to the present.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-rabkin05-295) After the [_Mariner_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_program "Mariner program") and [_Viking_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viking_program "Viking program") spacecraft had returned pictures of Mars as a lifeless and canal-less world, these ideas about Mars were abandoned; for many science-fiction authors, the new discoveries initially seemed like a constraint, but eventually the post-_Viking_ knowledge of Mars became itself a source of inspiration for works like [Kim Stanley Robinson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Stanley_Robinson "Kim Stanley Robinson")'s [_Mars_ trilogy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_trilogy "Mars trilogy").[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_note-296)

241.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars#cite_ref-243)**["Mariner 04"](https://solarsystem.nasa.gov/missions/mariner-04/in-depth). _NASA Solar System Exploration_. 20 December 2017. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20200803192306/https://solarsystem.nasa.gov/missions/mariner-04/in-depth/) from the original on 3 August 2020. Retrieved 9 February 2020. The Mariner 4 mission, the second of two Mars flyby attempts launched in 1964 by NASA, was one of the great early successes of the agency, and indeed the Space Age, returning the very first photos of another planet from deep space.![Image 52: Public Domain](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/62/PD-icon.svg/20px-PD-icon.svg.png) This article incorporates text from this source, which is in the [public domain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_domain "Public domain"). ["Spacecraft – Details - Mariner 4"](https://nssdc.gsfc.nasa.gov/nmc/spacecraft/display.action?id=1964-077A). _NASA – NSSDCA_. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20180904174225/https://nssdc.gsfc.nasa.gov/nmc/spacecraftDisplay.do?id=1964-077A) from the original on 4 September 2018. Retrieved 9 February 2020. Mariner 4...represented the first successful flyby of the planet Mars, returning the first pictures of the martian surface. These represented the first images of another planet ever returned from deep space.![Image 53: Public Domain](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/62/PD-icon.svg/20px-PD-icon.svg.png) This article incorporates text from this source, which is in the [public domain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_domain "Public domain").
